# Microsoft 365 Essential Training for Administrators

> Microsoft 365 is a bundled suite of SaaS applications and services for businesses. Once configured properly, the portfolio of products enhances an enterprise’s security and productivity and meets their compliance requirements. In this course, instructor Ed Liberman provides a thorough guide to all the Microsoft 365 features, capabilities, and opportunities. He clearly unpacks each major topic and 

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793) | 3h 42m | Intermediate | 6K learners

- [[Ed Liberman]]

- Microsoft 365

>

#### Benefits of cloud vs. on-premises
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=7)** Now I will tell you that there's a number of different categories we're going to look at here and in each one we're going to talk about how things may be currently with your on-premises environment and what it will look like if you went to a cloud environment.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=20)** So the first area is cost and maintenance.

> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=24)** On-premises, you have to understand that because you're going to have all of your data and all of your services on-premises, that you're going to have large upfront expenses.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=38)** You are going to have to purchase all the servers, you're going to have to purchase all the software and you may have to hire a significant amount of staff to manage the hardware and software depending on the size of your organization.
>

>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=56)** You have to buy the new faster server and you have to buy the new versions of software.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=63)** And there's also additional investments when it comes to malfunctions.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=68)** If something breaks, you have to pay to fix it or you have to pay to replace it because everything is owned by you.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=75)** Whereas with the cloud infrastructure, we have little to possibly no upfront costs.

> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=92)** But the flip side is you will have ongoing subscription fees that you otherwise wouldn't have on-premises, so some people look at that as a trade-off.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=101)** But the one benefit that I think cannot really be disputed is that maintenance and upgrades are the responsibility of the cloud provider.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=111)** You get to, for the most part, completely wash your hands of the need to pay attention for maintenance and upgrades.

> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=120)** Now, you may have a little bit of responsibility when it comes to upgrades because there may be some newer features that you'll have to decide if you want or not, but otherwise, traditional upgrades, that's all on the cloud provider.

>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=169)** So you get to have all the control but you also have all the responsibility.

> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=173)** And it also means that you're going to have to have a high level of security expertise.

> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=178)** And when I say you, I don't mean you personally necessarily as much as the organization will have to have someone who has a high level of security expertise, and that kind of goes back possibly even to the cost section that it can be costly hiring security experts.

> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=196)** Whereas in the cloud, the cloud provider is responsible for the security system.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=201)** So yes, you do have to give up some control, but if you can have trust in your cloud provider, there is the benefit of them having the responsibility of keeping you secure.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=214)** Most cloud providers offer comprehensive multi-layered security, which may be way more advanced than anything that you could implement yourself.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=226)** And there's typically global cybersecurity experts that will be involved.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=231)** Most of your larger cloud providers also have a global team of security experts who will be sure to keep everything safe.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=244)** Compliance.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=245)** On-premises, well, you're going to have to have specialized knowledge and expertise, and you do need to keep in mind that compliance is not something that you get to determine.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=255)** Yes, you may have internal policies that will need to have compliance, but there are also industry standards.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=263)** And if you're a global organization, there are different global standards that you will have to meet, so you have to be aware of how to do that.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=271)** And that can be quite costly, right?
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=274)** You may have to actually make purchases to implement certain things to put yourself in compliance.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=281)** Another big thing to keep in mind with compliance is that it's not a one and done.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=285)** You don't just set up your system, we're in compliance and that's it, we're done.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=289)** No, no, it's ongoing and regularly changing and you have to change as it changes.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=296)** And you are 100% responsible if it turns out that your organization is found in violation.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=304)** You have no one else to blame.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=306)** Whereas in a cloud infrastructure, the cloud provider takes on the majority of the burden.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=312)** And I'll come back to this in a moment, but I want to emphasize that it's the majority of the burden.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=316)** Not all the burden, but majority of it.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=319)** There again will be a global team of experts.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=323)** Okay, so just like with the security, we have a global team of cybersecurity experts.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=327)** Well, here we have a global team of compliance experts.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=331)** And I said I was going to come back to that issue of the majority of the burden.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=335)** You do want to be careful because ultimately, if your company is out of compliance, you can still be held responsible.
>
> **[5:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=343)** And you can't always just wash your hands of it and say "Well, but the cloud provider was supposed to do that."
>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=348)** Now you have to still have some awareness of compliance standards so that you can audit your own cloud provider to make sure that they are making you compliant.
>
> **[6:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=360)** When it comes to scalability, this one should be obvious by the way, as to the instant benefits to being in the cloud versus on-premises.
>
> **[6:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=367)** But to talk about this in detail, when you're on-premises, if you need to grow, you're going to have to go ahead and purchase additional resources.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=376)** It's going to take a lot of time, it's going to take a lot of money and may be inefficient if it's only a temporary growth because you'd have to actually buy something and then it just sits on a shelf when you no longer need it.
>
> **[6:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=389)** Whereas in the cloud, it is very simple.
>
> **[6:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=392)** Typically, it's just a few clicks to go ahead and tell your cloud provider that you want to go ahead and get more resources and they'll provide them for you instantly.
>
> **[6:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=401)** And it can be very efficient when it comes to temporary needs because you can click a few buttons to grow and then you can also very often go ahead and click a few buttons to say, "All right, I need to shrink."
>
> **[6:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=413)** That was only a temporary need.
>
> **[6:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=415)** All right, so it's zip, zip when it comes to scalability.
>
> **[6:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=418)** Definitely a lot of benefit to being a cloud infrastructure.
>
> **[7:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=422)** And then we have the reliability of data.
>
> **[7:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=425)** Well, I guess, on-premises, one benefit that could be looked at is you don't need internet to access data but the data will only be quickly available to the users that are actually on site.
>
> **[7:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=438)** Anybody that's remote, first of all, there'd have to be internet in order to be remote.
>
> **[7:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=442)** And then secondly, there'd have to be some form of VPN set up.
>
> **[7:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=446)** You will have additional costs for a storage system and for a backup system of that data.
>
> **[7:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=453)** And speaking of backup, if you have a loss of data, data recovery can be quite lengthy.
>
> **[7:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=459)** Whereas in a cloud infrastructure, you're going to be required to have a good, fast, reliable internet connection.
>
> **[7:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=466)** But as much as we may have decided that it was a benefit to not have internet on-premises, in today's world, having a good fast, reliable internet connection is pretty much standard everywhere anyway, okay?
>
> **[7:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=479)** So it's not really that big of a drawback.
>
> **[8:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=482)** Even a break in connectivity could delay access to data.
>
> **[8:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=486)** So again, potential negative there, but not much in today's world.
>
> **[8:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=490)** The good news is, is that the cloud provider will have all of the backup needs, so you don't have to worry about a loss of data.
>
> **[8:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=498)** And typically it's a shorter recovery time.
>
> **[8:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=501)** If you have data loss, the cloud provider is set up in a way to go ahead and provide a recovery of that data much faster than you could typically do it locally.
>
> **[8:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=513)** And finally, we have mobility.
>
> **[8:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=515)** Now, mobility can be a good choice if you have most of your users in the same office.
>
> **[8:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=523)** But as I mentioned when we were talking about reliability of data, a VPN may be necessary if you have remote workers who need to access that data.
>
> **[8:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=531)** Applications need to be regularly updated and it's not very flexible in the event of a natural disaster forces remote workers.
>
> **[9:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=540)** Now, we happen to have something that happened not that long ago, and that was that we had a recent pandemic worldwide that kind of put us in a position that people couldn't go to work.
>
> **[9:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=553)** They had to stay in their homes.
>
> **[9:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=555)** And so we're not very flexible in an on-premises infrastructure if people can't actually go to the office to be able to work in that infrastructure.
>
> **[9:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=566)** Whereas with a cloud infrastructure, users have access to data from anywhere as long as there's an internet connection.
>
> **[9:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=573)** So no VPNs are ever needed.
>
> **[9:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=576)** Your applications are always available and up to date and if mobility needs change, so again, if we talk about the pandemic where suddenly everyone doesn't come to the office, they all stay home, it's very flexible.
>
> **[9:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=588)** As long as they have an internet connection, we can go ahead and access everything, no problem.
>
> **[9:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/benefits-of-cloud-vs-on-premises?u=76281980&t=593)** So as you can see, there are a number of benefits that you could consider when moving from an on-premises infrastructure to a cloud infrastructure.

> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/adopting-microsoft-365?u=76281980&t=278)** Okay, so those are the tools that you need to have available to you if you are ready to go ahead and move your on-premises infrastructure to the Cloud.

#### Managing users

> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/configuring-multi-factor-authentication?u=76281980&t=293)** And now there's a QR code that in the Authenticator app, I would go ahead and I would scan, which would then tie the authenticator app on my phone if I were a demo user to this particular account in Microsoft 365.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/configuring-multi-factor-authentication?u=76281980&t=311)** And then going forward, every time the user goes to log in with their username and password, they would also have to have their phone with them and their authenticator app would go ahead and prompt them and say, did you just sign in?
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/configuring-multi-factor-authentication?u=76281980&t=324)** And then they would go ahead and confirm.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/configuring-multi-factor-authentication?u=76281980&t=326)** And that's how we have the multifactor authentication.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/configuring-multi-factor-authentication?u=76281980&t=329)** Now, in this case, I'm actually just going to stop here because demo user is not a real person.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/configuring-multi-factor-authentication?u=76281980&t=337)** There's not a real phone with an authenticator app to do all of this.
>
> **[5:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/configuring-multi-factor-authentication?u=76281980&t=341)** But that is the process that we would go through to go ahead and configure an account to have multifactor authentication in Microsoft 365.

#### Creating a hybrid identity scenario
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] You might find yourself in a situation where your organization needs to support a hybrid scenario.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=7)** So what is a hybrid scenario?
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=9)** Well, this is where you need to manage identity services both in an on-premises environment where you might use something like Active Directory Domain Services and then also a cloud-based environment like Microsoft 365 which uses Azure Active Directory.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=25)** So what's the solution? How do we do this?

>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=35)** First of all, please know that this is a directory services that has been around for a very long time.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=43)** It was actually first released with the Windows 2000 servers.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=47)** So yeah, it goes all the way back to the year 2000.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=51)** And it has primarily been used as the go-to on-premises identity and access management solution.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=59)** It is physically installed on a server, and that server is called a domain controller, and it is what manages all of the on-premises identities, such as users, computers, printers, things of that nature.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=73)** So why can't we use just one directory?
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=77)** Why do we need two directories?
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=80)** Well, the reason is because Active Directory is not compatible with cloud services.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=88)** It's only suitable for on-premises services.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=91)** So you might also be thinking, all right, well, then what about this Azure AD?
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=97)** I mean, that's the somewhat newer kid in town and that's the cloud-based directory services that we have out there.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=106)** Well, Azure AD only uses internet identity protocols and is not compatible with on-premises services, and that it's only suitable for the cloud services.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=121)** And that's why we have to have both directories, right?
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=124)** We have to have two directories, one that's for on-premises and one that is for the cloud.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=132)** Now, the solution to how we connect these two services and create our hybrid environment is with a tool called Azure AD Connect.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=141)** This is a tool that allows us to connect the on-premises and cloud environments together.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=148)** This can be on a permanent basis or temporary, maybe just as you migrate your systems out to the cloud.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=157)** Azure AD Connect allows your users to have one single identity that can be used for both on-premises and cloud-based systems.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=167)** And this is what we call hybrid identity.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=174)** Now, in order to use Azure AD Connect, there are some prerequisites.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=179)** So let me just kind of give it to you at a high level.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=184)** You first need to make sure that you have an Azure AD tenant, and this happens to be included with your Microsoft 365 Enterprise subscription.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=194)** You also need access to an online management portal, such as the Azure Portal.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=201)** You need to have added and verified your organization's custom domain, and you need to check for errors with your on-premises directory before you end up migrating out to the cloud.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=213)** And this check can be done with a tool called IdFix.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=220)** And once that tool has checked for any issues, then you can go ahead and configure synchronization options.
>
> **[3:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=230)** Now, after you have installed Azure AD Connect, you can use the wizard that it has built into it to configure the synchronization between Active Directory and your Azure Active Directory.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=248)** You can also modify the Azure AD settings.

>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=264)** Now, again, this is very high level.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=266)** You might be thinking, wait, where is all this?
>
> **[4:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=269)** Right now I just want you to understand the concept.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=272)** You can also configure how Azure AD Connect synchronizes the user objects stored within the directory.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=280)** For example, you could allow pass-through authentication or password hash synchronization, depending on your security requirements.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=289)** So the bottom line is that while you are migrating your way over from an on-premises environment over to the cloud, there may be some time where you may need this hybrid solution, where you'll have a little bit of both environments.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/creating-a-hybrid-identity-scenario?u=76281980&t=306)** And Azure AD Connect is the tool that will help get you there.

### 5. Microsoft 365 Security and Data

#### Microsoft Information Protection
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] You can implement Microsoft Information Protection, or MIP, to help you discover, classify, and protect sensitive information wherever it lives or travels.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=11)** MIP capabilities are included with Microsoft 365 compliance and give you the tools to know your data, to protect your data, and hopefully to prevent data loss.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=25)** Now, when it comes to knowing your data, to understand your data landscape, and identify important data across your hybrid environment, you want to use the following capabilities.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=38)** We have sensitive information types, which identify sensitive data by using built-in or custom regular expression or a function.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=48)** Corroborative evidence includes keywords, confident levels, and proximity.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=54)** We have trainable classifiers, which identify sensitive data by using examples of the data you're interested in, rather than identifying elements in the item or what we might call pattern matching.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=67)** You can use built-in classifiers or you could train a classifier with your own content.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=74)** And then we have data classification, which is a graphical identification of items in your organization that have a sensitivity label, a retention label, or have been classified.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=89)** Now to apply flexible protection actions, which can include encryption, access restrictions, and visual markings, you should use these capabilities.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=100)** We have sensitivity labels.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=103)** This is a single solution across apps, services, and devices to label and protect your data as it travels inside and outside your organization.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=114)** We have the Azure Information Protection unified labeling client, and this is where, when you have Windows computers, it extends sensitivity labels for additional features and functionality that includes labeling and protecting of all file types from File Explorer and PowerShell.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=134)** We have Double Key Encryption.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=137)** Under all circumstances, only your organization can ever decrypt protected content, or for regulatory requirements, you must hold encryption keys within a geographical boundary.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=152)** SharePoint Information Rights Management, or IRM, protects SharePoints lists and libraries so that when a user checks out a document, the downloaded file is protected so that only authorized people can view and use the file according to policies that you specify.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=173)** And finally, we have Cloud App Security, which discovers, labels, and protects sensitive information that resides in data stores that are in the cloud.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=184)** Now, if you want to help prevent accidental oversharing of sensitive information or data loss, here are some of the capabilities for you.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=193)** We have data loss prevention, or simply DLP, and this helps prevent unintentional sharing of sensitive items.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=201)** We have endpoint data loss prevention, which extends the DLP capabilities to items that are used and shared on Windows 10 or later computers.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=213)** Microsoft Compliance Extension extends the DLP capabilities to the Chrome browser, and you may want to protect sensitive information in Microsoft Teams chat and channel messages, which is basically an extension of the DLP functionality over to those teams chat and channel messages.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/microsoft-365-essential-training-for-administrators-22660793/microsoft-information-protection?u=76281980&t=235)** So again, you want to have a plan, and that plan is called Microsoft Information Protection, or MIP, and it's the three steps to simply know your data, protect your data, and therefore hopefully prevent data loss.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>

### 6. Microsoft 365 Threat Protection
